## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: The task describes the rate of change of concentration dA_dt as a function of time t and concentration A, which is the fundamental differential rate law in chemical kinetics. Typically dA/dt depends primarily on the current concentration A (autonomous ODE) with possible explicit time dependence due to catalyst deactivation or changing reaction conditions, leading to power-law, rational, or exponential structural forms common in that domain.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate independent of A)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (exponential decay of A)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular consumption of A)
- nth-order power law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general empirical reaction order, c1 can be negative for decay or positive for autocatalysis)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (linear with offset, from A <=> B equilibrium)
- Autocatalytic / logistic decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (rate peaks at intermediate A, typical of autocatalytic or epidemic-like reactions)
- Generalized rational kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + c2 * A) (saturation with two adjustable parameters)
- Saturation with exponent: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2**c1 + A**c1) (Hill-type sigmoidal rate, for cooperative binding or complex order)
- Catalyst deactivation with exponential time dependence: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate constant decays exponentially with time)
- Power-law time-dependent rate constant: dA_dt = c0 * A * t**c1 (e.g., gradual fouling or phase change effects)
- Combined zero- and first-order: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (quadratic rate law including reversible and autocatalytic terms)
- Two-exponential intermediate kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (rate as sum of exponentials when A is an intermediate in consecutive reactions, neglecting coupling back)
- Fractional-order with threshold: dA_dt = c0 * (A - c1)**c2 (rate only above threshold concentration c1, generalized power law)
- Logarithmic rate law: dA_dt = c0 * log(c1 * A) (rare but possible for highly diffusion-limited or fractal kinetics)
- Time-only external control: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * t + c2 * t**2 (polynomial rate representing programmed addition/removal independent of A)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Rate usually depends on concentration A (autonomous system); dominant patterns are monotonic decay dA/dt < 0 with A > 0, often power-law or rational.
- If dA/dt is independent of A (scatter independent of A), suggest zero-order kinetics or external time-dependent control.
- Linear dependence of dA/dt on A (positive slope) indicates first-order decay; an additional intercept suggests reversible reactions.
- Quadratic dependence dA/dt ∝ A^2 implies second-order or bimolecular consumption; quadratic with negative coefficient and peak at intermediate A suggests autocatalysis.
- Saturation behavior where dA/dt approaches a constant at high A (despite increasing A) is typical of enzyme-like Michaelis-Menten or Langmuir-Hinshelwood kinetics.
- Explicit time dependence in dA/dt (e.g., exponential attenuation of rate with t) often signals catalyst deactivation or environmental change.
- If rate is positive for some A and negative for others, there may be a stable equilibrium point where dA/dt = 0 (reversible or autocatalytic systems).
- Fractional exponents (e.g., A**0.5) indicate complex or fractal-like reaction mechanisms; a threshold (A - c) inside a power term hints at an induction period.
- For intermediates in consecutive reactions, dA/dt may consist of a difference of exponentials (production minus consumption) captured by a sum of exponential terms in t.
- Logarithmic or rational forms with multiple parameters often serve as empirical extensions for adsorption/desorption-controlled reactions or heterogeneous catalysis.
